  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9d24c9a6-05ca-4f2c-929e-88c76632fe14'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText4607257798590423975" style="display:none">Life is boring when you live in the real world, instead of starring in your own book series. Owen knows that better than anyone, what with the real world’s homework and chores.<br /><br />But everything changes the day Owen sees the impossible happen—his classmate Bethany climb out of a book in the library. It turns out Bethany’s half-fictional and has been searching every book she can find for her missing father, a fictional character.<br /><br />Bethany can’t let anyone else learn her secret, so Owen makes her a deal: All she has to do is take him into a book in Owen’s favorite Kiel Gnomenfoot series, and he’ll never say a word. Besides, visiting the book might help Bethany find her father…<br /><br />…Or it might just destroy the Kiel Gnomenfoot series, reveal Bethany’s secret to the entire world, and force Owen to live out Kiel Gnomenfoot’s final (very final) adventure.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1065473055" />
    <a title="Pinky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky"><img alt="Pinky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489855494p2/27523984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065473055?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pinky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pinky" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky">Pinky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27523984-pinky?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065473055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12312354969351082435">This is my first review!<br/><br/> This book is AMAZING! I knew that I wasn't going to be disappointed with this book. James Riley is my favorite author and when I heard this book was coming out, I was so pumped and excited! Story Thieves is so funny, it will have you laughing at many parts. <br/> I feel I can relate to all the characters in some way. There were so many quotes that I loved from this book. <br/> I was reading in the bus and there was a really funny part, so I started laughing. I didn't realize that </span>
  <span id="freeText12312354969351082435" style="display:none">This is my first review!<br /><br /> This book is AMAZING! I knew that I wasn't going to be disappointed with this book. James Riley is my favorite author and when I heard this book was coming out, I was so pumped and excited! Story Thieves is so funny, it will have you laughing at many parts. <br /> I feel I can relate to all the characters in some way. There were so many quotes that I loved from this book. <br /> I was reading in the bus and there was a really funny part, so I started laughing. I didn't realize that I was really loud until I looked up from the book. People were giving me concerned looks because they must have thought I was CRAZY. <br /> There was a huge plot twist and I never saw it coming. The writing was amazing. I never got bored in this book and I was laughing so much! It was just as amazing as Half Upon A Time! It was such a fun read!<br /> I felt that this book made me think about fictional characters. This book showed us how fictional characters would react if they found out that their entire life was being controlled by some random person,(author). It was so interesting to read something new and CREATIVE! <br /><br />Parts I loved!<br />•	“Half Upon A Time? I met that author once. He misspelled his own name in my book when he signed it. Weird.”<br />•	“The second rule they taught us in librarian school is that you can have as many favorite books as there are books.”<br />•	“Sit down,” she told him, pushing him into one of the chair’s seats. “Don’t be such a baby.”<br />“IT'S NOT BEING A BABY TO NOW WANT YOU DOING SURGERY ON ME!" <br />•	“This is my book?” Kiel said almost reverently, gently placing his fingers on the window. “I’m so …..Handsome! Look at me! Do you see this? Look!”<br />•	Ooh, you do look just like him!’ said a girl coming out of the store. ”that’s so cool!”<br />“Oh really?” Kiel said, posing beside the poster. “I mean, I’m probably a bit better looking, don’t you think? The painting loses something a little. But I can see the resemblance, I suppose.”<br />•	“The sad thing is,” she whispered to the girl, “he thinks he really is Kiel. It’s something wrong in his head. We just came to the author’s town to see if it might help snap him out of it.”<br /><br />There are a lot more parts that I enjoyed (Technically the whole book :)<br /><br /> I would give this book more than 5 stars, if I could. It is amazing and it is recommended for everyone!!!!!!! You could read this book by yourself, in a book club, with your family, or class! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12312354969351082435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3564613518" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3564613518" />
    <a title="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms"><img alt="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527940584p2/73227612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3564613518?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms " href="/user/show/73227612-tina-the-girl-who-lives-in-fandoms">Tina ➹ the girl who lives in Fandoms </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24521094-story-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3564613518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14131246691581616626"><b>4.5 Silver Stars</b><br/>With Golden Sparks!<br/><br/>I didn't want to read this book, wrong quick implication by seeing the word, "thieves" in the title & because it was middle grade, but then, one day earlier, it hit me like "you should read this!" beeb, beeb, beeb. middle grades are the best! (indeed they are, for my taste) & I immediately found the ebook & started reading it & I couldn't put it down.<br/>& I saw how wrong I was, what I would loss if I hadn't read it, this was brilliant & NOT at all the story I'd ex</span>
  <span id="freeText14131246691581616626" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Silver Stars</b><br />With Golden Sparks!<br /><br />I didn't want to read this book, wrong quick implication by seeing the word, "thieves" in the title &amp; because it was middle grade, but then, one day earlier, it hit me like "you should read this!" beeb, beeb, beeb. middle grades are the best! (indeed they are, for my taste) &amp; I immediately found the ebook &amp; started reading it &amp; I couldn't put it down.<br />&amp; I saw how wrong I was, what I would loss if I hadn't read it, this was brilliant &amp; NOT at all the story I'd expected! not even close!<br />it was another Great middle Grade to be added to my list of favourites.<br /><br />Once my friend &amp; I discussed that maybe in another life, we were the characters in our favourite books &amp; that’s why in this life we love them. (&amp; the authors were the main characters in there.)<br />It’s so fancy just to think about it. I love it, even if it’s so farfetched.<br />So here in this story, this idea was the closest thing I got to that interesting conversion. I was thrilled as a reader, as if the book was simultaneously be written as I read it. &amp; as an author I kept yelling at Owen that don’t mess with that story!<br />It was fun.<br />It was the fantasy version of ‘books about books’, story inside another story, &amp; it was brilliant!<br /><br />Owen, you dumba$$ cute enthusiastic fanboy, Authors do what they do because it’s something behind the curtains that you don’t know! So don’t mess with it. (it is my inner author shouting at Owen, not that I disagree, but still I’m happy he/they did it.) he also likes to reread &amp; finding clues &amp; he knows everything about the book. Yay!<br />I really liked Kiel, funny, arrogant in a good way, inspiring, hopeful.<br />My interest toward Bethany changed sinus-like, sometimes she was aggressive &amp; rude &amp; snapping at people, sometimes she was funny. How the fates (or should I say, the author) intertwined their path was funny &amp; making sense, in a fantasy middle-grade sort of sense.<br />Dr. Verity was hilarious too, I liked him.<br /><br />The writing style was fun, the inside thoughts, questions, sarcasms. Also unique, when it was needed. (&amp; I’m not kidding, I read the whole acknowledgement too, it was fun! he could be added to my fav authors list right away, but I should wait &amp; see.)<br />I was also enthralled to see all those book references. (･ω･)<br />&amp; I was reminded of my first Potterhead years when I was waiting for the new books in the series to come. Especially last book. good old times...<br />I also started watching "Once Upon a Time" as I needed something to watch with modernized nowadays version world &amp; medieval fairytale fantasy &amp; it is awesome too.<br /><br />It was a quick read, once I blinked, I noticed I read 10 chapters! Action-packed, hilarious fantasy book about books. I really enjoyed it.<br /><br />&amp; again, I would like to read Kiel's all 7 books! gimme them!<br /><br /><br />Plot: ★★★★/5<br />Characters: ★★★★/5<br />Writing style: ★★★★/5<br />World Building: ★★★★/5<br />general idea: ★★★★/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="14131246691581616626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1170082623" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1170082623" />
    <a title="Stuti (Turmeric isn&#39;t your friend. It will fly your ship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6372822-stuti-turmeric-isn-t-your-friend-it-will-fly-your-ship"><img alt="Stuti (Turmeric isn&#39;t your friend. It will fly your ship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458489431p2/6372822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1170082623?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuti (Turmeric isn&#39;t your friend. It will fly your ship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuti (Turmeric isn&#39;t your friend. It will fly your ship" href="/user/show/6372822-stuti-turmeric-isn-t-your-friend-it-will-fly-your-ship">Stuti (Turmeric isn&#39;t your friend. It will fly your ship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6372822-stuti-turmeric-isn-t-your-friend-it-will-fly-your-ship?shelf=fantasy-pr-everything-untoward">fantasy-pr-everything-untoward</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6372822-stuti-turmeric-isn-t-your-friend-it-will-fly-your-ship?shelf=more-please">more-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6372822-stuti-turmeric-isn-t-your-friend-it-will-fly-your-ship?shelf=recipe-for-awesomesauce">recipe-for-awesomesauce</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1170082623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16124626517050802311"><b>4.5</b> <br/><br/><i>And then everything exploded into fire and chaos and awesome.</i><br/><br/>Ha! is all I want to say to my 2014 self. HA! With <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22546584.Story_Thieves__Story_Thieves___1_' title='Story Thieves (Story Thieves, #1) by James Riley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Story Thieves</a>, I've come to fully embrace the new year. I think. See, last year I picked up my kindle to read the book, only to put it down in favor of reading Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows. AGAIN. Which I don't regret but later on, and blah blah blah, you don't care, I don't.<br/><br/>Whatever.<br/><br/>What do I say? Ummm... this is totally an awesome book! I haven't fangirled so hard about a</span>
  <span id="freeText16124626517050802311" style="display:none"><b>4.5</b> <br /><br /><i>And then everything exploded into fire and chaos and awesome.</i><br /><br />Ha! is all I want to say to my 2014 self. HA! With <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22546584.Story_Thieves__Story_Thieves___1_" title="Story Thieves (Story Thieves, #1) by James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Story Thieves</a>, I've come to fully embrace the new year. I think. See, last year I picked up my kindle to read the book, only to put it down in favor of reading Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows. AGAIN. Which I don't regret but later on, and blah blah blah, you don't care, I don't.<br /><br />Whatever.<br /><br />What do I say? Ummm... this is totally an awesome book! I haven't fangirled so hard about anything besides Game of Thrones and Calculus* in recent memory, going so far as to do some ninja-style-dancing which prompted my brother to kick me. He's the real ninja. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22546584.Story_Thieves__Story_Thieves___1_" title="Story Thieves (Story Thieves, #1) by James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Story Thieves</a>, in as pretentious terms as I can manage, is a story about the differences between reality and fiction, <i>and</i> lack thereof. Simply put: Owen, he who sits in math class and loves to fanboy hard, gets a chance to save the hero of his hero, and then play the part of his hero. Bethany, she who skirts the edges of fun, after much cajoling and running and shouting and saving the world, finally gives in and acts a bit fictional to save reality.<br /><br />In all, it's a clever and emotional and action-packed book with characters as similar to you and me as can be if we were all tweens (I think) who hated math. <br /><br /><i>"It worked. And it worked because I embraced the problems and made it work for me.That's real magic."<br />"<b>No.</b> Real magic is when you make something happen that's physically impossible."<br />"Well, sure, that too. That's real magic. But this is real<b>er</b> magic."<br />"No, it's not that either. The word doesn't even exist."<br />"So, in a away, that word is magic, by your definition."</i><br /><br />It pokes fun and fingers through cliches and tropes about story characters, then full-on embraces them. Hell, the story makes use of plot holes to complete the plot. And hats off to THAT!<br /><br />More to the point: There are side characters whose full depths we perhaps never truly realize until we confront them ourselves--that's what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4337106.James_Riley" title="James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">James Riley</a> shows, in the fictional world in his fictional story within this fictional story. <br /><br />Owen plays the part of Kiel Gnomenfoot, dying and being saved by dumb luck, solely on the conviction that it's a book, and nothing truly bad can happen. However, as he plods along, it turns out that the book gets progressively darker. And in the end, it's the reality that he's faced, has lived in, has conditioned him which ends up saving him.<br /><br />And Bethany, who is half-fictional and can dive into stories, becomes a little more fictional in her life. Embraces the impossible.<br /><br /><i>"You don't ever speak to me again, do you understand? And if you ever tell anyone about me, I'll find the deepest, darkest math book I can find, and drop you into the most boring part!"</i><br /><br />She's truly formidable.<br /><br />Like I said: clever, clever book. Not the clever of books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6948436.Little_Bee" title="Little Bee by Chris Cleave" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Bee</a> but you know, I found kernels of secrets and irony and realism that even now make me giggle. <br /><br />The story within the story is, from a space-eagle's perspective with poor eyesight, about an inter-planetary war between Magisteria, world of magic and imagination and chaos, and Quanterium, world of science and order and innovation. It's a thought-out, quirky world and I truly appreciated the fact that I got to finish its story, that the author had me invested in it so fast, so hard.<br /><br />It's funny, sad, poignant and full of awesome. These are characters you understand, who make you laugh and smile and giggle all in one breath, whom you sometimes would prefer to throw out of the book. They're not as fleshed out and/or complicated as the last what? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15905.Thomas_Hardy" title="Thomas Hardy" rel="nofollow noopener">Thomas Hardy</a> book you read. But I loved it. I loved it. And you should read it tooooooooooo!<br /><br />There ARE so many plotholes and questions I'd like to ask and consequences that weren't dealt with but I think the last was kinda one of the points of this ordeal our characters went through and to the rest, well I still love it, don't I?<br /><br />There are tidbits about life and librarians, too.<br /><br /><i>"Don't worry. Maybe you just haven't found your favorite book yet. I honestly don't think anyone has. Just when you think you might have a favorite, something better comes along."</i><br /><br />So true. (Also <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7417780.The_Piper_s_Son" title="The Piper's Son by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">The Piper's Son</a> or gtfo.)<br /><br />#Kiel_Gnomenfoot4Life<br /><br /><i>"I'm really happy to have gotten to know you."</i><br /><br /><i>Thank you thank you thank you to the people at Aladdin who rose up like a genie from a bottle in mist and clouds and fog, to present the best book I've read in 2015 so far.</i><br /><br />*Probably, Owen and Bethany won't be big fans of mine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16124626517050802311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2149405-gisbelle?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1006882400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13416523519777820531"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409451088i/10981266.jpg' width='300' height='60' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>My thanks to <b>
  <i>Aladdin</i>
</b> & Edelweiss<br/><br/>------------------------------------------------------------------<br/><b>Point of View</b>: Dual (Owen & Bethany)<br/><b>Writing</b>: Third Person | Past Tense<br/><b>Setting</b>: N/A<br/><b>Genre</b>: Middle Grade | Fantasy<br/>------------------------------------------------------------------<br/><br/><b>It was a wonderful book right from the start until the very end</b>. The storyline was refreshing and so full of action that it kept me on the edge of the seat. I loved how the story progress, from such a measly simple thing </span>
  <span id="freeText13416523519777820531" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409451088i/10981266.jpg" width="300" height="60" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>My thanks to <b>
  <i>Aladdin</i>
</b> &amp; Edelweiss<br><br>------------------------------------------------------------------<br><b>Point of View</b>: Dual (Owen &amp; Bethany)<br><b>Writing</b>: Third Person | Past Tense<br><b>Setting</b>: N/A<br><b>Genre</b>: Middle Grade | Fantasy<br>------------------------------------------------------------------<br><br><b>It was a wonderful book right from the start until the very end</b>. The storyline was refreshing and so full of action that it kept me on the edge of the seat. I loved how the story progress, from such a measly simple thing to an adventurous journey in the hope of saving the day. I can't wait to find out their next encounter. <br><br><b>The characters were well-developed</b>; I loved them all! Bethany was a tough little girl, and Owen was just an adorable goofball. Together, they made quite a pair. <br><br><b>The book was written in a way that completely captured my attention. </b>Its pace was really great as it wasn't moving way too fast or too slow as I normally find in most middle grade books I have read. The storyline was full of excitement and nail-biting suspense that it was hard not to read the whole thing in one sitting. The humor added a fascinating touch to the story, making reading this book was delightful experience.<br><br>All in all, I absolutely adored this book. <b>The appealing characters, humors dialogues and the witty storyline </b>were just a few things I loved about this book. I'm sure a lot of people will enjoy this book as much as I did. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Yingling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Yingling" href="/user/show/2636606-ms-yingling">Ms. Yingling</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194670180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8632575384955518963">Owen loves the fantasy books series about Kiel Gnomenfoot and is looking forward to the last book in the series. When he starts to notice that a girl in his class, Bethany, is acting very suspiciously in class and at the public library, where his mother works, he watches her closely and discovers that she can leap in to stories! When he confronts her, she admits that her father was fictional, and that she jumped into a story given to her at a birthday party when she was very young, and manages t</span>
  <span id="freeText8632575384955518963" style="display:none">Owen loves the fantasy books series about Kiel Gnomenfoot and is looking forward to the last book in the series. When he starts to notice that a girl in his class, Bethany, is acting very suspiciously in class and at the public library, where his mother works, he watches her closely and discovers that she can leap in to stories! When he confronts her, she admits that her father was fictional, and that she jumped into a story given to her at a birthday party when she was very young, and manages to drag her father there and lose him. She's been forbidden from jumping into stories, but does anyway because they are far more interesting than real life. Owen agrees, and begs to go with her, especially since he wants to find out what happens to the Magister in the last Kiel book. Once they get in to the book, however, things go wrong and Owen gets trapped while Kiel gets trapped in the real world. Difficulties also arise with characters that seem to be good who are actually evil, and Owen endangers Kiel's world by pretending to be him but not having the knowledge. Bethany would like to be able to find her father, and Owen hopes he can help, but will they manage instead to endanger both the fictional and the real worlds?<br />Strengths: Nods to Harry Potter will make this a good book to hand to students who can't move beyond that series. Fairly solid world building, decent characters, and lots of action and adventure.<br />Weaknesses: Bethany's quest felt like the most important one in the book, yet it didn't get as much attention as I hoped. The ending lends itself to a sequel, so we'll see. <br />What I really think: Personally painful, but at least I got a lot of work done around the house. Scrub the bathroom, or finish this book? Scrub. Trim the dog's behind or finish the book? Trim. I'm uncertain whether I will buy this for my avid fantasy fans, so will try the ARC on a couple. For elementary readers who love fantasy, this would be a great choice. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8632575384955518963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_992902764" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/992902764" />
    <a title="BookLoversLife" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4020075-bookloverslife"><img alt="BookLoversLife" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515879985p2/4020075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/992902764?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BookLoversLife" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BookLoversLife" href="/user/show/4020075-bookloverslife">BookLoversLife</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4020075-bookloverslife?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4020075-bookloverslife?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4020075-bookloverslife?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer992902764" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14254312470715040509">For Owen, life is boring. He longs for something exciting to happen, like his favourite character Kiel Gnomenfoot, well he is in for a big surprise! When he is in the library helping his mother, he sees a book on the floor. Just as he goes to pick it up he sees the book moving and then, impossibly, a hand coming out of it. Next thing he knows, his classmate, Bethany pops out. <br/><br/>He learns that Bethany is half fictional, her father popped out of a book and fell in love with her mother. When Bethany </span>
  <span id="freeText14254312470715040509" style="display:none">For Owen, life is boring. He longs for something exciting to happen, like his favourite character Kiel Gnomenfoot, well he is in for a big surprise! When he is in the library helping his mother, he sees a book on the floor. Just as he goes to pick it up he sees the book moving and then, impossibly, a hand coming out of it. Next thing he knows, his classmate, Bethany pops out. <br /><br />He learns that Bethany is half fictional, her father popped out of a book and fell in love with her mother. When Bethany was little she accidentally jumped her whole party into a book and lost her father. She is afraid that something happened to him for him no to come back out and is now searching every and any book to find him. Owen cant believe the possibilities and is thrilled!! He tells Bethany that he will help her and he knows a spell that may help find her father, all they have to do is jump into the Kiel Gnomenfoot book and read the spell from the spell book. Bethany agrees on the condition that Owen follows the rules!! But can Owen follow the rules? What happens if he just says one thing to a character or tries to save someone?<br /><br />Well this was such a fun read!! This is my first book by this author but it wont be my last. The Story Thieves is an engaging and action packed read and one that all ages will enjoy. <br /><br />I loved the plot so much. Who wouldn't love to be able to actually jump into their favourite stories. Could you imagine how awesome that would be!!! <br /><br />The characters were a breath of fresh air. Bethany has a magical gift but she doesn't abuse it. She knows the rules and sticks to them. When Owen sees her and what she can do, she freaks at first but thinks that it might be nice to have a friend to help. She started out as so nervous but her character developed so much throughout the book. <br /><br />Owen was such a cutie, he was so fun to read. He wants to be like his favourite character Kiel but is it all its cracked up to be? When Bethany tells him the rules he cant see the harm of trying to save someone, whats the worst that can happen?? His name may appear in the book, which would be ultra cool, right!! Wrong. Owen sets things in motion that he cant control! Even when he messes up, Owen will do the right thing. I loved his enthusiasm and his joy of seeing the characters. <br /><br />The friendship in the book was awesome. Bethany and Owen start out slowly because Bethany is afraid he will think she is crazy. Then Bethany and Kiel are thrown together and have the world to save while Own is thrown into the fictional world and has to save that! <br /><br />Every character was well written and developed, even the fictional characters. I loved Kiel! He was such a snarky fun character even if he is fictional within the fictional story ;). The plot within the plot I enjoyed as well. I loved the Kiel Gnomenfoot books and would so read them! I loved the fact that we are dealing with two separate plots but both intertwine. It was a unique and fun thing to read. <br /><br />Overall The Story Thieves was a fast paced and fun read. I read it with my boys and they loved the idea of jumping into books. They were discussing what books they would love to visit and I loved that! Its a book within a book and while aimed at the middle grade audience there's still enough of a plot for everyone to enjoy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14254312470715040509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2105006544" />
    <a title="Yasmeena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70796687-yasmeena"><img alt="Yasmeena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602362119p2/70796687.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781508228899" href="/book/show/30312920-story-thieves">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2105006544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13858743112836265907">A little backstory: I first found this book in the Scholastic book fair in my school in 4th grade. I saw the summary and I was interested. It seemed to me that out of all the books in that colorful catalog, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22546584.Story_Thieves__Story_Thieves___1_' title='Story Thieves (Story Thieves, #1) by James Riley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Story Thieves</a> was the only one that popped out. That showed. You see what I mean? BUT. Being the dim-witted 4th grader I was, I didn’t buy it.<br/><br/>A few months ago, I was in Barnes and Noble. I saw <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22546584.Story_Thieves__Story_Thieves___1_' title='Story Thieves (Story Thieves, #1) by James Riley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Story Thieves</a> in the juvenile fiction section. I thought this was my opportunity to experience how I</span>
  <span id="freeText13858743112836265907" style="display:none">A little backstory: I first found this book in the Scholastic book fair in my school in 4th grade. I saw the summary and I was interested. It seemed to me that out of all the books in that colorful catalog, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22546584.Story_Thieves__Story_Thieves___1_" title="Story Thieves (Story Thieves, #1) by James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Story Thieves</a> was the only one that popped out. That showed. You see what I mean? BUT. Being the dim-witted 4th grader I was, I didn’t buy it.<br /><br />A few months ago, I was in Barnes and Noble. I saw <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22546584.Story_Thieves__Story_Thieves___1_" title="Story Thieves (Story Thieves, #1) by James Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Story Thieves</a> in the juvenile fiction section. I thought this was my opportunity to experience how I’d read this in 4th grade. Then, I bought it.<br /><br />As soon I started reading it, I immediately regret why I hadn’t bought this sooner. <b>This book is <i>amazing.</i></b> I started relying on the book fair from now on, since there might be another one of my favorite books.<br /><br />I have to say, this is hands down my favorite book of all time. It was waaaaay better than I'd expected. Not gonna lie, about 100 pages in the first time, I wanted to stop because I kinda lost interest, so I took a brief break. Later, I decided, <i>Oh, I'll try more.</i> <br /><br />I don't regret that decision, because I kept going, and that book, like changed my life. I mean, Story Thieves is all I talk about in dinner, I chose Story Thieves for an assignment in English where we have to analyze the hero's journey (I got a 100 btw), and just...look at my profile picture.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <u>People, go ahead and buy this book already.</u>
  </i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_1165990234" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165990234" />
    <a title="Jaina Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19291001-jaina-rose"><img alt="Jaina Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414283304p2/19291001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1165990234?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaina Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaina Rose" href="/user/show/19291001-jaina-rose">Jaina Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19291001-jaina-rose?shelf=blogged">blogged</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165990234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3240906585352161698">This review is also available on my blog, <a href='http://ireadtilldawn.blogspot.com/2015/03/story-thieves-by-james-riley-2015.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Read Till Dawn</a>.<br/><br/>Hmm. I'm not really sure what to say about this one. Did I love it? Did I hate it? Well, neither. Not yet, anyway.<br/><br/>The plot seems all over the place at times, but it actually comes together pretty cohesively by the end of the book. My main trouble, when I really come down to it, is the characters. Bethany especially just isn't particularly realistic. She's more of a stock character: she's got magical powers, one of her parents is missing/de</span>
  <span id="freeText3240906585352161698" style="display:none">This review is also available on my blog, <a href="http://ireadtilldawn.blogspot.com/2015/03/story-thieves-by-james-riley-2015.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Read Till Dawn</a>.<br /><br />Hmm. I'm not really sure what to say about this one. Did I love it? Did I hate it? Well, neither. Not yet, anyway.<br /><br />The plot seems all over the place at times, but it actually comes together pretty cohesively by the end of the book. My main trouble, when I really come down to it, is the characters. Bethany especially just isn't particularly realistic. She's more of a stock character: she's got magical powers, one of her parents is missing/dead, she has this huge secret she hides from the rest of the world, and on and on. The fact that she's been going into books for years behind her mother's back for years makes her, to me at least, a little too dishonest to really be that sympathetic. I also felt like there was no way she'd really open up to some random classmate the way she did, and I seriously started questioning her judgement when she agreed to take Owen into the Kiel Gnomenfoot series. I mean, hello? What did she think was going to happen if she took this kid into his all-time favorite book series? She did get better as the story went along, though. Bethany didn't exactly become my favorite character in the world, but I have hope for her development in the later books. Riley has prepared some great set-ups for the next books, and if I had to guess he'll make me absolutely adore Bethany, Owen, and Kiel (who, by the way, is probably my favorite character yet) by the end of the series.<br /><br />And that's really the crux of this review: I think this book is a set-up for the books ahead. If Riley does a wonderful job with the later books (as I'm 95% sure he will, based on his Half Upon a Time trilogy), then someday I'll look back at Story Thieves and have a ball reading through it again, because there will be all sorts of hints and foreshadowing that I totally missed without foreknowledge. I'll go back to retrace the beginnings of whatever relationships Riley chooses to favor in the later books (my money's totally on Bethany and Kiel!), and watch characters in a different light because I know what secrets they're hiding, or what will happen to them down the road. In a few years, I think I'll love Story Thieves because it is a beginning of a new series by a writer who is amazing at making me laugh, cry, and fall in love. Until then, this is a so-so book that makes an okay standalone, one that holds potential but no concrete prize. The best part was probably the ending, because it sets the stage for awesomeness in the second book.<br /><br />If you want to read a James Riley, I recommend starting with his wonderful Half Upon a Time series. Story Thieves has potential, but doesn't hold a candle to Riley's crazy-fun fairy-tale spin-off. Of course, that could change - like I said, everything hinges on the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3240906585352161698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1965837826" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1965837826" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9083576-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588116997p2/9083576.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1965837826?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/9083576-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9083576-emily?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9083576-emily?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1965837826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4291589000505292247">To be quite honest, I have NO idea where to start. I'm not entirely exactly certain if I even LIKED the book or not. I'll probably read the next one just to see? Maybe that means I did like it? Don't know. I can see some middle-graders loving it.<br/><br/>First of all, I don't understand what exactly the title is referring to. I thought it meant that the MCs would be stealing parts of stories for some purpose. There was a little character thievery going on, but it's a bit of a stretch to call it "Story Th</span>
  <span id="freeText4291589000505292247" style="display:none">To be quite honest, I have NO idea where to start. I'm not entirely exactly certain if I even LIKED the book or not. I'll probably read the next one just to see? Maybe that means I did like it? Don't know. I can see some middle-graders loving it.<br /><br />First of all, I don't understand what exactly the title is referring to. I thought it meant that the MCs would be stealing parts of stories for some purpose. There was a little character thievery going on, but it's a bit of a stretch to call it "Story Thieves". <br /><br />Second, there was a scientific mistake in that one of the characters stated that gold doesn't conduct electricity. Gold DOES. And middle-graders study that, so they'll either catch the mistake, or a misconception will be perpetuated in their mind. As a former science teacher, I saw some glimpses of red in my peripheral vision. The other science was correct, so I don't see it only not doing that in the fictional world? Because science was a huge part of said fictional world. A disclaimer, at the least, would have been nice. Like the character from reality mentioning that it does conduct in his world or something.<br /><br />THIRD. This could be pro OR con, depending on the reader. This story moves at an absolutely BREAKNECK pace. There is no time to process, or catch one's breath. Each chapter switches POVs, and due to the pacing, can be interesting to keep straightened out with everything that is going on. <br />It was definitely a page-turner, and held my attention, but I had a lot of WHAT IN THE WORLD IS GOING ON?! moments, as well. There are also a few horror aspects to it, especially in the last few chapters, so I wouldn't recommend it to more sensitive readers.<br /><br />Whirlwind of a book. 3 out of 5 stars. Long review for someone who didn't know where to start and uses the word "first" when she DOES start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4291589000505292247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1161621103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18350431385443650132">STORY THIEVES by James Riley is an action-packed fantasy that blurs the line between real life and fictional worlds. <br/><br/>What if you could literally dive into a good book? Bethany can. As the child of a real mother and fictional father, she’s able to disappear into any paper book. Bethany has spent years carefully exploring library books for her lost father. When Owen discovers her secret, they begin an adventure that breaks the “fourth wall” mixing the real world with fantasy universes. <br/><br/>This clever</span>
  <span id="freeText18350431385443650132" style="display:none">STORY THIEVES by James Riley is an action-packed fantasy that blurs the line between real life and fictional worlds. <br /><br />What if you could literally dive into a good book? Bethany can. As the child of a real mother and fictional father, she’s able to disappear into any paper book. Bethany has spent years carefully exploring library books for her lost father. When Owen discovers her secret, they begin an adventure that breaks the “fourth wall” mixing the real world with fantasy universes. <br /><br />This clever new fantasy series will be a hit with a wide range of book lovers including those who enjoy fairy tales, magic stories, and science fiction. With many references to popular works of fiction, youth will be drawn into the premise and easily imagine themselves in the shoes of the main characters.<br /><br />Known for his fractured fairy tales, James Riley provides just the right balance of action and suspense to keep readers engaged in the story. He skillfully weaves together silly subplots, humorous dialogue, and witty references into a storyline perfect for middle grade readers. Youth will easily empathize with the well-developed characters who have dreams and desires that sometimes get in the way of making good choices.<br /><br />Fans of books like Fablehaven and Inkheart will enjoy the book’s premise, while science fiction and steampunk fans will love the characters from Owen’s favorite fictional series.<br /><br />Like Bethany and Owen, your children will want to dive into this exciting fantasy adventure.<br /><br />Edelweiss ARC used for review<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18350431385443650132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1061964869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1061964869" />
    <a title="Frank Chillura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34993279-frank-chillura"><img alt="Frank Chillura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410838626p2/34993279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1061964869?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frank Chillura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frank Chillura" href="/user/show/34993279-frank-chillura">Frank Chillura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34993279-frank-chillura?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1061964869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8745511973056638974">When reading the synopsis for this book, I was a little hesitant in starting it. It sounds an awful lot like the premise of Inkheart. Well, in Inkheart, the main character can read characters into or out of a book, where as in Story Thieves, the main character can pull people or characters into or out of the book with her. Seeing as how I am a huge fan of Inkheart, I didn't want to be comparing the two stories the entire time I was reading. Sometimes I find that when I see a similarity, comparin</span>
  <span id="freeText8745511973056638974" style="display:none">When reading the synopsis for this book, I was a little hesitant in starting it. It sounds an awful lot like the premise of Inkheart. Well, in Inkheart, the main character can read characters into or out of a book, where as in Story Thieves, the main character can pull people or characters into or out of the book with her. Seeing as how I am a huge fan of Inkheart, I didn't want to be comparing the two stories the entire time I was reading. Sometimes I find that when I see a similarity, comparing is the only thing I can do. For this review, I will attempt to not compare as much as possible.<br /><br />To middle schooler, Owen, nothing is more exciting than opening up one of his favorite books &amp; imagining himself a part of the story... but it isn't until he discovers his classmate Bethany can go in to the stories she is reading that his dreams actually start seeming like they may come true. All he has to do is trick her into bringing him into his favorite series, Kiel Gnomenfoot, so he can save the day and become the hero he knows he is. While all Bethany is trying to do is find her missing father.<br /><br />But little does he know, nothing ever happens exactly like you imagine. In a serious of accidental events, the characters from the story are released into the real world &amp; the only way to make sure that the story goes on is for him to disguise himself as the main character, Kiel. His every dream is coming true... adventure is on the horizon. But adventure is NOT all its cracked up to be.<br /><br />While Owen is off gallivanting at being a hero, Bethany is stuck trying to round up fictional characters in the real world before someone finds out her secret. <br /><br />One part Inkheart, One part Harry Potter, &amp; One part Steampunk, Story Thieves is sure to appeal to the middle schoolers and older who are looking for a good release into action &amp; adventure. If you have ever dreamed of being a part of the stories you have read &amp; love, then this is a great book for you to pick up. <br /><br />If you are looking for any other book or series suggestions, feel free to message me through my blog UtopiaNeverComes.blogspot.com or email me at FooFiFauxPaw@google.com. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8745511973056638974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<div id="review_2003867452" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2003867452" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/291872-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1255380005p2/291872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2003867452?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/291872-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545900874" href="/book/show/25352646-story-thieves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/291872-thomas?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2003867452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12952835070752019995">Story Thieves was an impulse buy, something I found on the shelves at Target and figured it was worth a shot. It sounded a little like a kids' version of Jasper Fforde's Thursday Next series, and as much as I like that series, it was a no-brainer. Maybe I should have recognized that I would see the book as derivative, and left it alone.<br/><br/>It's about Owen, an avid reader who finds the regular world boring. He wishes his life were more like Kiel Gnomenfoot, the central character of his favorite serie</span>
  <span id="freeText12952835070752019995" style="display:none">Story Thieves was an impulse buy, something I found on the shelves at Target and figured it was worth a shot. It sounded a little like a kids' version of Jasper Fforde's Thursday Next series, and as much as I like that series, it was a no-brainer. Maybe I should have recognized that I would see the book as derivative, and left it alone.<br /><br />It's about Owen, an avid reader who finds the regular world boring. He wishes his life were more like Kiel Gnomenfoot, the central character of his favorite series of books (think Harry Potter, but a lot more arrogant), and when he discovers that one of his classmates has the ability to go inside books and live in their worlds, of course he has to find a way into the Kiel Gnomenfoot books so he can meet his hero. Once inside, he can't help but get involved, which throws the book off the rails and sets into motion a series of events that threatens more than just Kiel Gnomenfoot's world.<br /><br />The book isn't bad, really, but it's hard to care much about the three central characters. Owen is obnoxious and duplicitous, since he has to trick his classmate, Bethany, into bringing him into the books, and Kiel is arrogant and self-centered. Bethany is the closest thing to being sympathetic, but it feels like she's pushed aside for the two boys' stories. Owen's story takes place without her, and though she's involved with Kiel's story, his use of magic makes him the active player in their conflict. She's integral to the story -- she's the one with the power to go in and out of books, after all -- and she's the smartest of the three, but I wish she'd received more of a share of the action. The characters grow over the course of the story, but it's hard hanging in long enough to get to that point.<br /><br />I waffled over giving the book two or three stars, and ultimately went with three, rounding up from two-and-a-half. I would recommend it to kids who like clever fantasy stories, but adults might find it lacking. I'll move on to the next book (I've already placed the hold on it through the library), so I hope it improves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12952835070752019995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15875228809380455259">Owen lives in the world of his favorite books – at least in his mind. But when he meets Bethany emerging from a book, he realizes he might be able to do that for real. Despite Bethany’s strict rules, Owen tricks her into going and changing the outcome of the sixth Kiel Gnomefoot book. However, the consequences are more than he bargained for.   <span id="freeText15875228809380455259" style="display:none">Owen lives in the world of his favorite books – at least in his mind. But when he meets Bethany emerging from a book, he realizes he might be able to do that for real. Despite Bethany’s strict rules, Owen tricks her into going and changing the outcome of the sixth Kiel Gnomefoot book. However, the consequences are more than he bargained for. Will he and Bethany be able to return things to the way they should be?<br /><br />Having dreamed of jumping into books myself, I loved the premise of this book even before I read it. It delivered on the promise in spades. I wasn’t super impressed with the Kiel Gnomefoot story within the story, but that was a minor complaint. The plot overall was very engrossing and the characters were fun. I can’t wait to see what happens to Owen and Bethany next.<br /><br />Read my full review at <a href="http://carstairsconsiders.blogspot.com/2015/02/book-review-story-thieves-by-james.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Carstairs Considers</a>.</span>

  <span id="freeText10413565379500139922" style="display:none">Oh my. This book was so good, I could have read it in a day-but due to school <br />(and parents who want you to get a good night's sleep), I had to finish this book at the beginning of school.<br /><br />Five complete, total, brilliant stars for Story Thieves.<br /><br />________________________________<br /><br />At first: This is interesting, I guess, but--WHAT?! I finished 20% of the book already?! Maybe it's a short book.<br /><br />Middle: *turns pages at lightning speed*<br /><br />End: Oh my. Oh my. Oh my. BOOK TWO!! HERE I COME!!!!<br /><br />________________________________<br /><br />And that basically sums it up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10413565379500139922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14526097609221180905"><br/>True rating: 4.5 stars.<br/><br/>A terrific read. Riley makes fun of the 'Harry Potter' genre, and I mean, he <i>MAKES</i> FUN! Winning characters, tongue-in-cheek jokes, a rollicking plot, and much more, add up to a heap o' reading pleasure. Though, thankfully, this was not one of those series starters that leave you with a cliffhanger, enough threads remain dangling to make the reader long for the next book. Very well done!<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4284666284435683574">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Every readers dream! This started out a bit slow and then characters were making stupid decisions (I had to keep reminding myself that they were kids and trying not to judge them too harshly). But once we got to them trying to fix their mistakes, I was on board and enjoyed it. I really liked Owen's relationship with Charm, and Bethany's relationship with Kiel. I'm happy that most of the same characters will be back for book 2. <br/><br/>Kirby Heyborne does a great job with the audio version. </span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gdavgPr5vzMq6CYkbPbQrVAyBi+0NE5d8TcxWfSFbSAzDT8T3aij6gkeSbWbss1oHD3MO3J3U8G0+U6oKo/VxQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U9MZa96kEoEb4FhkMIySNvE1ZYT4FLbDEAZhqH8bNHfhCIn4+fUOWDgWN/XHyI/zvTqvkD5Xq19VyB5ZoRGMkg==')})
  }
